2:25:1483:0:14:72:404:700:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:Product Mix and Firm Productivity Responses to Trade Competition 
2:26:1547:14:14:72:371:686:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:Thierry Mayer, Marc J. Melitz, and Gianmarco I.P. Ottaviano 
2:27:1606:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 22433
2:28:1634:14:14:72:243:658:12:Times:12:g_d0_f2:July 2016, Revised December 2016
2:29:1666:14:28:72:157:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. D24,F12
2:30:1681:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:31:1689:28:14:72:543:588:12:Times:12:Times:We  document  how  demand  shocks  in  export  markets  lead  French  multi-product  exporters  to  re-
2:32:1792:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:allocate the  mix  of  products  sold  in  those  destinations.  In  response  to  positive  demand  shocks, 
2:33:1900:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:those  French firms  skew  their  export  sales  towards  their  best  performing  products;  and  also 
2:34:2003:14:14:71:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:extend the range of products sold to that market. We develop a theoretical model of multi-product 
2:35:2100:14:14:71:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:firms   and   derive   the specific   demand   conditions   needed   to   generate   these   product-mix 
2:36:2204:14:14:71:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:reallocations.  These  demand  conditions are  associated  with  endogenous  price  elasticities  that 
2:37:2306:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:satisfy  Marshall's  Second  Law  of  Demand  (the price  elasticity  of  demand  decreases  with 
2:38:2403:14:14:71:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:consumption).   Under   these   demand   conditions,   our   theoretical model   highlights   how   the 
2:39:2506:14:14:71:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:increased  competition  from  demand  shocks  in  export  markets  –  and  the  induced product  mix 
2:40:2606:14:14:71:545:462:12:Times:12:Times:reallocations  –  induce  productivity  changes  within  the  firm.  We  then  empirically  test for  this 
2:41:2712:14:14:71:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:connection between the demand shocks and the productivity of multi-product firms exporting to 
2:42:2805:14:14:72:545:434:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:those destinations. We find that the effect of those demand shocks on productivity are substantial 
2:43:2903:14:28:72:542:420:12:Times:12:Times:– and explain an important share of aggregate productivity fluctuations for French manufacturing.
2:44:3000:28:14:72:142:392:12:Times:12:Times:Thierry Mayer
2:45:3013:14:14:72:161:378:12:Times:12:Times:Sciences-Po, Paris
2:46:3031:14:14:72:198:364:12:Times:12:Times:Department of Economics

2:48:3077:14:14:72:129:336:12:Times:12:Times:75007 Paris
2:49:3088:14:14:72:105:322:12:Times:12:Times:France
2:50:3094:14:14:72:179:308:12:Times:12:Times:and CEPII, and CEPR
2:51:3113:14:28:72:215:294:12:Times:12:Times:thierry.mayer@sciences-po.fr
2:52:3141:28:14:72:142:266:12:Times:12:Times:Marc J. Melitz

2:65:3386:14:14:306:387:308:12:Times:12:Times:United Kingdom
2:66:3400:14:14:306:515:294:12:Times:12:Times:and University of Bologna, CEP and CEPR

3:68:3462:0:32:72:166:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:1  Introduction
3:69:3477:32:20:72:540:677:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Recent studies using detailed micro-level datasets on firms, plants, and the products they produce
3:70:3575:20:20:72:540:657:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:have documented vast differences in all measurable performance metrics across those different units.
3:71:3675:20:21:72:540:637:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Those studies have also documented that these performance differences are systematically related to
3:72:3774:21:20:72:540:616:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:participation in international markets (see, e.g., Bernard, Jensen, Redding and Schott (2007, 2012)
3:73:3873:20:20:72:540:596:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for the U.S., and Mayer and Ottaviano (2008) for Europe):  Exporting firms and plants are bigger,
3:74:3970:20:21:72:540:576:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:more productive, more profitable, and less likely to exit than non-exporters.  And better performing
3:75:4070:21:20:72:540:555:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms and plants export a larger number of products to a larger number of destinations.  Exporters
3:76:4168:20:20:72:540:535:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are larger in terms of employment, output, revenue and profit.  Similar patterns also emerge across
3:77:4267:20:20:72:540:515:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the set of products sold by multi-product firms.  There is a stable performance ranking for firms
3:78:4364:20:21:72:540:495:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:based  on  the  products’  performance  in  any  given  market,  or  in  worldwide  sales.   Thus,  better
3:79:4470:21:20:72:540:474:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:performing products in one market are most likely to be the better performing products in any
3:80:4563:20:20:72:540:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:other market (including the global export market).  This also applies to the products’ selection into
3:81:4664:20:21:72:492:434:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a destination, so better performing products are also sold in a larger set of destinations.
3:82:4755:21:20:88:539:413:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Given  this  heterogeneity,  trade  shocks  induce  many  different  reallocations  across  firms  and
3:83:4857:20:20:72:540:393:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:products. Some of these reallocations are driven by ‘selection effects’ that determine which products
3:84:4958:20:21:72:540:373:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are sold where (across domestic and export markets), along with firm entry/exit decisions (into/out
3:85:5057:21:20:72:540:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of any given export market, or overall entry/exit of the firm).  Other reallocations are driven by
3:86:5155:20:20:72:540:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:‘skewness effects’ whereby – conditional on selection (a given set of products sold in a given market)
3:87:5257:20:21:72:540:312:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:– trade affects the relative market shares of those products.  Both types of reallocations generate
3:88:5356:21:20:72:540:291:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(endogenous) productivity changes that are independent of ‘technology’ (the production function
3:89:5451:20:20:72:512:271:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at the product-level).  This creates an additional channel for the aggregate gains from trade.
3:90:5545:20:21:88:539:251:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Unfortunately,  measuring  the  direct  impact  of  trade  on  those  reallocations  across  firms  is  a
3:91:5650:21:20:72:540:230:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:very  hard  task.   On  one  hand,  shocks  that  affect  trade  are  also  likely  to  affect  the  distribution
3:92:5763:20:20:72:540:210:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  market  shares  across  firms.   On  the  other  hand,  changes  in  market  shares  across  firms  likely
3:93:5873:20:21:72:540:190:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reflect  many  technological  factors  (not  related  to  reallocations).   Looking  at  reallocations  across
3:94:5983:21:20:72:540:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:products within firms obviates many of these problems.  Recent theoretical models of multi-product
3:95:6081:20:20:72:540:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms highlight how trade induces a similar pattern of reallocations within firms as it does across
3:96:6180:20:21:72:540:129:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms.   And  measuring  reallocations  within  multi-product  firms  has  several  advantages:   Trade
3:97:6283:21:20:72:540:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks that are exogenous to individual firms can be identified much more easily than at a higher
3:98:6380:20:0:72:540:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:level of aggregation;  Controls for any technology changes at the firm-level are also possible;  and
4:99:6481:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reallocations  can  be  measured  for  the  same  set  of  narrowly  defined  products  sold  by  the  same
4:100:6588:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firm across destinations or over time.  In addition, impediments to factor reallocations are likely
4:101:6687:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to be substantially higher across firms than across product lines within firms.  Moreover,  multi-
4:102:6785:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:product  firms  dominate  world  production  and  trade  flows.   Hence,  reallocations  within  multi-
4:103:6888:21:20:72:540:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:product firms have the potential to generate large changes in aggregate productivity.  Empirically,
4:104:6987:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we find very strong evidence for the effects of trade shocks on those reallocations, and ultimately
4:105:7086:20:21:72:540:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on the productivity of multi-product firms.  The overall impact on aggregate French manufacturing
4:106:7183:21:20:72:200:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:productivity is substantial.
4:107:7211:20:20:88:539:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  rest  of  the  paper  is  organized  as  follows.   Section  2  briefly  surveys  the  recent  empirical
4:108:7320:20:21:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:literature  on  trade-induced  reallocations.   Section  3  introduces  our  dataset  on  French  exporters
4:109:7427:21:20:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and provides novel evidence on such reallocations with a special emphasis on skewness effects.  It
4:110:7525:20:20:72:540:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shows  that  positive  demand  shocks  in  any  given  destination  market  induce  French  exporters  to
4:111:7630:20:21:72:540:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:skew their product level export sales to that destination towards their best performing products.
4:112:7727:21:20:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:These  demand  shocks  also  lead  to  strong  positive  responses  in  both  the  intensive  and  extensive
4:113:7835:20:20:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:margins of export sales to that destination.  Section 4 introduces a flexible theoretical framework
4:114:7934:20:21:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with multi-product firms to rationalize all this empirical evidence.  Our framework highlights how
4:115:8032:21:20:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:certain properties of demand – which relate to the curvature of the demand and marginal revenue
4:116:8127:20:20:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:curves – are crucial in generating predictions for reallocations that are consistent with the data.
4:117:8226:20:21:72:540:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In particular, these empirically relevant properties rule out the case of constant elasticity demand.
4:118:8327:21:20:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:They also imply that positive demand shocks engender increases in multi-product firm productivity
4:119:8424:20:20:72:540:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:since  those  shocks  induce  firms  to  produce  relatively  more  of  their  better  performing  products
4:120:8531:20:21:72:540:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(the  skewness  effect).   Sections  5  and  6  take  these  predictions  to  the  data  and  measure  large
4:121:8639:21:20:72:540:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:responses in multi-product firm productivity to demand shocks in export markets.  We find that
4:122:8733:20:20:72:540:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:these productivity responses explain an important share of aggregate productivity fluctuations for
4:123:8831:20:37:72:180:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:French manufacturing.
4:124:8852:37:31:72:392:184:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:2  Previous Evidence on Trade-Induced Reallocations
4:125:8903:31:21:72:540:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In a previous paper, Mayer, Melitz and Ottaviano (2014), we investigated, both theoretically and
4:126:8999:21:20:72:540:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:empirically, the mechanics of product reallocations within multi-product firms across export desti-
4:127:9098:20:20:72:540:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:nation markets. We used comprehensive firm-level data on annual shipments by all French exporters
4:128:9195:20:20:72:540:92:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to all countries in the world (not including the French domestic market) for a set of more than
4:129:9290:20:0:72:540:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:10,000 goods.  Firm-level exports are collected by French customs and include export sales for each
5:130:9390:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:8-digit (combined nomenclature or NC8) product by destination country.  Our focus then was on
5:131:9483:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the cross-section of firm-product exports across destinations (for a single year, 2003).  We presented
5:132:9585:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:evidence that French multi-product firms indeed exhibit a stable ranking of products in terms of
5:133:9681:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:their shares of export sales across export destinations with ‘core’ products being sold in a larger
5:134:9780:21:20:72:540:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:number of destinations (and commanding larger market shares across destinations).  We used the
5:135:9874:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:term ‘skewness’ to refer to the concentration of these export market shares in any destination and
5:136:9972:20:21:72:540:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:showed  that  this  skewness  consistently  varied  with  destination  characteristics  such  as  GDP  and
5:137:10078:21:20:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:geography:  French  firms  sold  relatively  more  of  their  best  performing  products  in  bigger,  more
5:138:10185:20:20:72:540:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:centrally-located destinations (where competition from other exporters and domestic producers is
5:139:10281:20:21:72:116:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tougher).
5:140:10290:21:20:88:539:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Other  research  has  also  documented  similar  patterns  of  product  reallocations  (within  multi-
5:141:10392:20:20:72:540:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:product firms) over time following trade liberalization.  For the case of CUSFTA/NAFTA, Baldwin
5:142:10487:20:21:72:540:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and Gu (2009), Bernard, Redding and Schott (2011), and Iacovone and Javorcik (2010) all report
5:143:10581:21:20:72:540:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that Canadian, U.S., and Mexican multi-product firms reduced the number of products they pro-
5:144:10674:20:20:72:540:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:duce during these trade-liberalization episodes.  Baldwin and Gu (2009) and Bernard, Redding and
5:145:10770:20:21:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Schott (2011) further report that CUSFTA induced a significant increase in the skewness of pro-
5:146:10865:21:20:72:540:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:duction across products.  Iacovone and Javorcik (2010) separately measure the skewness of Mexican
5:147:10962:20:20:72:540:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms’ export sales to the US. They report an increase in this skewness following NAFTA: They
5:148:11055:20:21:72:540:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:show that Mexican firms expanded their exports of their better performing products (higher mar-
5:149:11150:21:20:72:540:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ket shares) significantly more than those for their worse performing exported products during the
5:150:11247:20:20:72:283:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:period of trade expansion from 1994−2003.
5:151:11288:20:21:88:539:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:As prices are rarely observed, there is little direct evidence on how markups, prices and costs
5:152:11383:21:20:71:539:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are  related  across  products  supplied  with  different  productivity,  and  how  they  respond  to  trade
5:153:11491:20:20:71:539:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:liberalization.1A  notable  exception  is  the  recent  paper  by  De  Loecker,  Goldberg,  Pavcnik  and
5:154:11595:20:21:71:539:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Khandelwal (2016) who exploit unique information on the prices and quantities of Indian firms’
5:155:11689:21:20:71:539:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:products over India’s trade liberalization period from 1989−2003.  They also document that better
5:156:11786:20:20:71:539:180:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:performing firms (higher sales and productivity) produce more products,  before focusing on the
5:157:11881:20:21:71:539:160:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:evidence for firm and product level markups.  Across firms, they show that those better performing
5:158:11979:21:20:71:539:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms also set higher markups.  They also document a similar pattern across the products produced
5:159:12076:20:16:71:539:119:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by  a  given  multi-product  firm,  which  sets  relatively  higher  markups  on  their  better  performing
5:160:12183:16:0:84:539:103:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:1Prices are typically backed-out as unit values based on reported quantity information, which is extremely noisy.
6:161:12297:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:products (lower marginal cost and higher market shares).2In addition, they show strong evidence
6:162:12392:21:20:71:539:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for endogenous markup adjustments via imperfect pass-through from products’ marginal costs to
6:163:12485:20:20:71:539:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:their prices:  Only a portion of marginal cost decreases are passed on to consumers in the form of
6:164:12583:20:21:71:539:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lower prices, while the remaining portion goes to higher markups.  This is consistent with recent
6:165:12680:21:20:71:539:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firm-level evidence on exchange rate pass-through.  Berman, Martin and Mayer (2012) analyze the
6:166:12775:20:20:71:539:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:heterogeneous reaction of French exporters to real exchange rate changes across destinations over
6:167:12872:20:21:71:539:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a decade (1995−2005).  They find that on average firms react to depreciation by increasing their
6:168:12968:21:20:71:539:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:markup.  They also find that high-performance firms increases their markup significantly more –
6:169:13063:20:20:71:478:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:implying that the pass-through rate is significantly lower for better performing firms.
6:170:13150:20:21:88:539:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Berman, Martin and Mayer (2012) also find very strong evidence that this pass-through rate
6:171:13240:21:20:71:539:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(the elasticity of price with respect to the exchange rate) is heterogeneous across firms:  it sharply
6:172:13342:20:20:71:539:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:decreases with firm performance (better performing firms adjust their markups substantially more
6:173:13438:20:21:71:539:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:than worse performing firms in response to the same exchange rate shock).  Li, Ma and Xu (2015)
6:174:13533:21:20:71:539:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:confirm this result of decreasing pass-through (with firm performance) for Chinese exporters. Amiti,
6:175:13633:20:20:71:539:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Itskoki, and Konings (2014) also find a very similar result for Belgian firms, whereby pass-through
6:176:13732:20:21:71:539:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is strongly decreasing with the Belgian firms’ export market share.  Chatterjee, Dix-Carneiro, and
6:177:13830:21:20:71:539:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Vichyanond (2013) also show this pattern for Brazilian exporters.  In addition, they find that this
6:178:13929:20:20:71:539:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:property of decreasing pass-through also holds within multi-product Brazilian firms across their set
6:179:14029:20:21:71:539:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of exported products.  That is, they find substantially lower pass-through rates for a firm’s better
6:180:14129:21:20:71:356:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:performing products (with relatively higher market shares).
6:181:14188:20:20:88:539:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This evidence on prices, markups, and pass-through is directly related to properties of demand
6:182:14282:20:21:71:539:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(such as its elasticity).  We review those connections when we introduce our theoretical model and
6:183:14380:21:20:71:539:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:its demand properties.  We will then show that the same demand properties are required to generate
6:184:14478:20:20:71:539:241:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the product reallocations that we document in the following section.  This provides an independent
6:185:14576:20:38:71:402:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:source of confirmation for the evidence based on product-level prices.
6:186:14646:38:31:71:237:183:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3  Reallocations Over Time
6:187:14672:31:20:71:540:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We now document how changeswithina destination market over time induce a similar pattern of
6:188:14763:20:20:71:539:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reallocations as the ones we previously described (holding across destinations).  More specifically,
6:189:14863:20:16:71:539:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we show that demand shocks in any given destination market induce firms to skew their product
6:190:14956:16:15:84:539:96:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:2Using product-level prices for multi-product firms, Dhyne et al (2016) also document a strong correlation between
6:191:15070:15:0:72:246:81:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:a product’s sales rank and its productivity.
7:192:15115:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:level  export  sales  to  that  destination  towards  their  best  performing  products.   In  terms  of  first
7:193:15226:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:moments,  we  show  that  these  demand  shocks  also  lead  to  strong  positive  responses  in  both  the
7:194:15333:20:36:72:392:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:intensive and extensive margins of export sales to that destination.
7:195:15401:36:27:72:127:632:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:3.1  Data
7:196:15410:27:20:72:540:605:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We  use  the  same  data  source  for  firm  exports  (described  in  Section  2)  as  Mayer,  Melitz  and
7:197:15516:20:21:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Ottaviano  (2014),  extended  to  cover  multiple  years  from  1995-2005.   All  firms  operating  in  the
7:198:15623:21:20:72:540:564:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:French  metropolitan  territory  must  report  their  export  sales  according  to  the  following  criteria:
7:199:15732:20:20:72:539:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Exports to each EU destination whenever within-EU exports exceeds 100,000 Euros;3and exports
7:200:15824:20:21:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to non-EU country whenever exports to that destination exceeds 1,000 Euros or a ton.  Despite
7:201:15917:21:20:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:these limitations, the database is nearly comprehensive.  For instance, in 2005, 103,220 firms report
7:202:16018:20:20:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:exports across 234 destination countries (or territories) for 9873 products.  This represents data on
7:203:16119:20:21:72:200:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:over 2.2 million shipments.
7:204:16146:21:20:88:539:442:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We restrict our analysis to firms whose main activity is classified as manufacturing to ensure
7:205:16240:20:20:72:540:422:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that firms take part in the production of the goods they export.4This leaves us with data covering
7:206:16338:20:21:72:423:402:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:more than a million shipments by firms across all manufacturing sectors.5
7:207:16411:21:20:88:539:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Matched balance-sheet data provide us with information on variables that are needed to assess
7:208:16504:20:20:71:539:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firm productivity such as turnover,  value added,  employment,  investment,  raw material use and
7:209:16601:20:21:71:539:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:capital.  However, we can only measure product reallocations in terms of sales in export markets
7:210:16697:21:20:71:539:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as  the  breakdown  of  sales  across  products  for  the  domestic  market  is  not  available  to  us.   We
7:211:16806:20:20:71:539:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:will have to take this into account in designing our estimation strategy.  The balance-sheet data
7:212:16903:20:21:71:539:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we  have  access  to  comes  in  two  sources  where  the  official  identification  number  of  the  firm  can
7:213:17014:21:20:71:539:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be  matched  with  customs  information.   The  first  source  is  the  EAE,  produced  by  the  national
7:214:17119:20:20:71:539:239:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:statistical institute, and exhaustive for manufacturing firms with size exceeding 20 employees.  The
7:215:17219:20:21:71:539:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:second is BRN, which comes from tax authorities, and includes a broader coverage of firms, since it
7:216:17318:21:15:71:539:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is based on the firm’s legal tax regime and a relatively low sales threshold.  Whenever firm data is
7:217:17418:15:15:84:539:183:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:3If this threshold is not met,  firms can choose to report under a simplified scheme without supplying separate
7:218:17529:15:11:72:540:168:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:EU export destinations.  However, in practice, many firms under the threshold report their exports by destination.
7:219:17643:11:11:72:540:157:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:During our sample period, the threshold increased from 38,050 Euros (250,000 French Francs) to 100,000 Euros in
7:220:17754:11:11:72:540:146:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:2001.  We have checked that all our results are robust to using only the 1996-2001 subsample (a sample period that
7:221:17868:11:7:72:428:135:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:also features a more stable product classification schedule; See Pierce and Schott, 2012).
7:222:17958:7:11:84:530:128:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:4Some large distributors such as Carrefour account for a disproportionate number of annual export shipments.
7:223:18066:11:15:84:539:117:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:5In a robustness check, we also drop observations for firms that report an affiliate abroad.  This avoids the issue
7:224:18181:15:11:72:540:102:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:that multinational firms may substitute exports of some of their best performing products with affiliate production in
7:225:18299:11:11:72:540:91:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:the destination country (affecting our measurement of product reallocations).  Results are quantitatively very similar
7:226:18417:11:0:72:141:80:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:in all regressions.
8:227:18437:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:available from both sources, we give precedence to the EAE data (which is more closely monitored
8:228:18533:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by the statistical authorities).6Table 1 provides some descriptive statistics relevant to the match
8:229:18632:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:between customs and balance sheet data.  The overall match is not perfect but covers between 88
8:230:18727:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and 95 percent of the total value of French exports.  The match with firms declaring manufacturing
8:231:18825:21:20:72:540:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as their main activity is still very good although there is a clear trend of declining quality of match,
8:232:18929:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:particularly after 2000.  This is also visible in the aggregate growth rate of exports in our sample
8:233:19029:20:21:72:540:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(column 5) that overall provide a quite good match of the overall exports growth rate in column
8:234:19124:21:20:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(4), but deteriorating over time.  Our investigations suggest that the increasing propensity of large
8:235:19225:20:20:72:540:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:French manufacturers to declare their main activity as retail or some other service activity might
8:236:19323:20:21:72:539:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:provide part of that explanation.7Overall our matched dataset is very comparable to recent papers
8:237:19420:21:20:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:using the same primary sources as in by Eaton et al.  (2011), Berman et al.  (2012) or di Giovanni
8:238:19518:20:32:72:194:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:et al.  (2014) for instance.

8:259:20713:28:15:84:539:151:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:6The correlations between variables reported both in EAE and BRN (value added, employment, exports, capital
8:260:20820:15:7:72:289:136:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:stock) are very high:  between .91 and .99 in all cases.
8:261:20876:7:0:84:458:129:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:7This is another reason why we check all our results against the early 1996-2001 sub-sample.
9:262:20969:0:28:72:292:709:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:3.2  Measuring Export Demand Shocks
9:263:21004:28:20:72:540:681:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Consider a firmiexporting a number of productssin industryIto destinationdin yeart.  We
9:264:21091:20:20:71:540:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:measure  industries  (I)  at  the  3-digit  ISIC  level  (35  different  classifications  across  French  manu-
9:265:21202:20:21:71:539:641:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:facturing).  We consider several measures of demand shocks that affect this export flow.  At the
9:266:21298:21:20:71:540:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:most aggregate level we use the variation in GDP ind, log GDPd,t.  At the industry levelI, we use
9:267:21395:20:20:72:540:600:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:total imports intodexcludingFrench exports, logMId,t.  We can also use our detailed product-level
9:268:21492:20:37:72:353:580:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shipment data to construct a firmi-specific demand shock:
9:269:21549:37:37:106:540:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:trade shockIi,d,t≡logMsd,tfor all productss∈Iexported by firmitodin yeart0,(1)
9:270:21627:37:20:72:540:506:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:whereMsd,trepresents  total  imports  intod(again,  excluding  French  exports)  for  productsand
9:271:21724:20:21:72:540:486:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the overline represents the (unweighted) mean.  For world trade, the finest level of product level of
9:272:21825:21:20:72:540:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:aggregation is the HS-6 level (from UN-COMTRADE and CEPII-BACI)8, which is more aggregated
9:273:21915:20:20:72:540:445:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:than our NC8 classification for French exports (roughly 5,300 HS products per year versus 10,000
9:274:22011:20:21:72:540:425:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:NC8 products per year).  The construction of the last trade shock is very similar to the one for
9:275:22107:21:20:72:540:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the industry level imports logMId,t, except that we only use imports intodfor the precise product
9:276:22204:20:20:72:539:384:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:categories that firmiexports tod.9In order to ensure that this demand shock is exogenous to the
9:277:22299:20:21:71:539:364:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firm, we use the set of products exported by the firm in its first export year in our sample (1995,
9:278:22398:21:20:71:539:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:or later if the firm starts exporting later on in our sample), and then exclude this year from our
9:279:22496:20:20:71:539:323:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:subsequent analysis.  Note that we use an un-weighted average so that the shocks for all exported
9:280:22593:20:21:71:396:303:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:productss(within an industryI) are represented proportionately.10
9:281:22658:21:20:88:540:282:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:For all of these demand shocksXt= GDPd,t,MId,t,Msd,t, we compute the first difference as the
9:282:22750:20:20:71:539:262:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Davis-Haltiwanger growth rate: ̃∆Xt≡(Xt−Xt−1)/(.5Xt+.5Xt−1).  This measure of the first
9:283:22837:20:21:71:539:242:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:difference preserves observations when the shock switches from 0 to a positive number, and has a
9:284:22933:21:20:71:540:221:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:maximum growth rate of−2 or 2.  This is mostly relevant for our measure of the firm-specific trade
9:285:23031:20:20:71:540:201:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shock, where the product-level imports intod,Msd,tcan often switch between 0 and positive values.
9:286:23128:20:16:71:540:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:WheneverXt−1,Xt>0, ̃∆Xtis monotonic in ∆ logXtand approximately linear for typical growth
9:287:23217:16:11:84:218:165:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:8See Gaulier and Zignago (2010).
9:288:23249:11:15:84:539:154:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:9There is a one-to-many matching between the NC8 and HS6 product classifications,  so every NC8 product is
9:289:23355:15:11:72:540:139:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:assigned  a  unique  HS6  classification.   We  use  the  sameMsd,tdata  for  any  NC8  productswithin  the  same  HS6
9:290:23473:11:7:71:124:128:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:classification.
9:291:23488:7:15:80:539:121:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:10Thus,  positive  idiosyncratic  demand  shocks  to  high  market-share  products  (which  mechanically  contribute  to
9:292:23608:15:11:71:539:106:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:increase  the skewness of  product  sales)  are given  the  same  weight as  positive  idiosyncratic  shocks  to low  market-
9:293:23733:11:11:71:539:95:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:share products (which mechanically contribute to decrease the skewness of product sales); and vice-versa for negative
9:294:23850:11:0:71:100:84:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:shocks.
10:295:23858:0:18:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rates (|∆ logXt|<2).11We thus obtain our three measures of demand shocks in first differences:
10:296:23952:18:23:73:539:691:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4: ̃∆GDPd,t, ̃∆MId,t, ̃∆Msd,t.  From here on out, we refer to these three shocks, respectively, as GDP
10:297:24052:23:20:71:539:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shock, trade shock – ISIC, and trade shock.  Note that this last firm-level shock, ̃∆Msd,t, represents
10:298:24154:20:36:72:503:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the un-weighted average of the growth rates for all products exported by the firm int−1.
10:299:24242:36:27:72:452:612:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:3.3  The Impact of Demand Shocks on Trade Margins and Skewness
10:300:24304:27:21:72:540:585:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Before focusing on the effects of the demand shocks on the skewness of export sales, we first show
10:301:24402:21:20:72:540:564:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:how the demand shocks affect firm export sales at the intensive and extensive margins (the first
10:302:24498:20:20:72:540:544:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:moments of the distribution of product export sales).  Table 2 reports how our three demand shocks
10:303:24596:20:21:72:540:524:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(in first differences) affect changes in firm exports to destinationdin ISICI(so each observation
10:304:24693:21:20:72:540:503:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:represents a firm-destination-ISIC combination).  We decompose the firm’s export response to each
10:305:24790:20:20:72:540:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shock into an intensive margin (average exports per product) and an extensive margin (number of
10:306:24885:20:21:72:540:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:exported products).  We clearly see how all three demand shocks induce very strong (and highly
10:307:24979:21:20:72:540:442:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:significant) positive responses for both margins.  This confirms that our demand shocks capture
10:308:25074:20:32:72:396:422:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:important changes in the local demand faced by French exporters.12

11:330:26584:0:21:88:539:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We now investigate the consequences of those demand shocks for the skewness of export sales
11:331:26675:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(independent of the level of product sales).  In Mayer, Melitz and Ottaviano (2014), we focused on

11:333:26871:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:within a destination over time using our new demand shocks.  We rely on the Theil index as our

11:335:27064:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at the destination-ISIC level up to the firm-level – in order to generate predictions for firm-level
11:336:27164:20:21:72:539:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:productivity.  Thus, our measure of skewness for the distribution of firmi’s exports to destination

12:423:29869:11:11:180:432:430:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:FE refers to firm-destination-ISIC fixed effects.  All regressions
12:424:29935:11:11:180:432:419:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:include year dummies, and standard errors clustered at the level
12:425:29999:11:33:180:287:408:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:of the destination country.
12:426:30026:33:20:72:539:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The parameterηis often called the inequality aversion parameter as higher values put more weight
12:427:30122:20:20:72:540:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on the low end of the distribution. Whenηgets close to 0, more weight is given to high values, in our
12:428:30223:20:21:72:540:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:case to the firm’s best performing products.  Asηincreases, more weight is given to the distribution
12:429:30323:21:20:72:540:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the firm’s worse performing products relative to the best performing ones.  This Atkinson index is
12:430:30424:20:20:72:540:294:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:also equal to one minus the ratio of the generalized (CES) mean over the arithmetic mean.  Different
12:431:30524:20:20:72:539:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:values ofηprovide different special cases of the generalized mean:  withη= 2, it is the harmonic
12:432:30620:20:21:72:539:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mean, whereas withη= 1 it is the geometric mean.  In the limit, whenη= 0, it is the arithmetic
12:433:30714:21:20:72:540:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:mean, in which case there can never be any inequality (AI,ηi,d,t≡0 for any distribution of product
12:434:30812:20:20:72:539:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:salesxsidt).  Table 4 reproduces our skewness results for a wide range of inequality parametersη,
12:435:30909:20:21:72:540:193:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:starting with a low value ofη=.5 along with the special cases ofη= 1 andη= 2.14Those results,
12:436:31002:21:20:72:540:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reported in columns (2-4), clearly show that the effect of the demand shocks on skewness do not
12:437:31097:20:20:72:508:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rely on the Theil functional form nor on a specific weighing scheme for the Atkinson index.
12:438:31188:20:21:88:539:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The skewness measures in Table 4 combine changes to both the intensive product mix margin
12:439:31277:21:16:72:540:111:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(the relative sales of different products exported in botht−1 andt),  and the extensive margin

12:441:31494:15:0:72:199:80:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:evaluation of income inequality.

14:466:32832:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(products  sold  in  one  period  but  not  the  other).   We  now  isolate  the  skewness  response  that  is
14:467:32942:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:driven only by the intensive product mix margin.  To do this, we recompute the skewness measures

14:469:33129:20:21:71:539:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with a “const” superscript).  Results using these intensive margin skewness measures are reported

14:471:33322:20:20:71:539:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:intensive  margin:  the  sales  ratio  (in  logs)  of  the  firm’s  best  to  second  best  performing  product
14:472:33433:20:21:71:539:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(in terms of global export sales).  The effect of our firm-level trade shock is significant across all
14:473:33535:21:20:71:539:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:these specifications (and significant well beyond the 1% level for all the distribution wide skewness
14:474:33636:20:20:71:539:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:measures).  The intensive margin skewness results for the ISIC-level trade shock and the GDP shock
14:475:33734:20:38:71:447:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are always positive and significant in most (but not all) of those specifications.
14:476:33816:38:31:71:228:488:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:4  Theoretical Framework
14:477:33840:31:20:71:539:457:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In the previous section we documented the pattern of product reallocations in response to demand
14:478:33936:20:21:71:539:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks in export markets. We now develop a theoretical model of multi-product firms that highlights
14:479:34035:21:20:71:539:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the  specific  demand  conditions  needed  to  generate  this  pattern.   We  show  that  these  demand
14:480:34138:20:20:71:539:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conditions  are  consistent  with  all  of  the  micro-level  evidence  on  firm/product  selections,  prices,
14:481:34248:20:20:71:539:376:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and markups presented in section 2.  In particular, those demand conditions highlight how demand
14:482:34344:20:21:71:539:356:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks lead to changes in competition for exporters in those markets (which lead to the observed
14:483:34440:21:20:71:539:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reallocations).   Those  reallocations,  in  turn,  generate  changes  in  firm  productivity.   We  directly
14:484:34549:20:20:71:539:315:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:investigate  the  empirical  connection  between  demand  shocks  and  productivity  in  the  following
14:485:34652:20:21:71:111:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sections.
14:486:34661:21:20:88:539:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our theoretical model contributes to the growing literature emphasizing demand systems with
14:487:34752:20:20:71:539:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variable price elasticities for models of trade.15Our main point of departure relative to those papers
14:488:34854:20:21:71:539:234:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is that we seek to connect the demand conditions on variable elasticities (and further properties
14:489:34951:21:20:71:539:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  demand)  directly  to  the  evidence  on  the  product  reallocations  that  we  document;  and  our
14:490:35055:20:20:71:539:193:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:additional goal of empirically connecting those to firm-level productivity.  In this spirit, our paper
14:491:35157:20:21:71:539:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is most closely related to Arkolakis et al (2015) and Asplund and Nocke (2006), who also directly
14:492:35254:21:20:71:539:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:connect their theoretical modeling of endogenous markups with empirical moments:  Arkolakis et
14:493:35348:20:20:71:539:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:al (2015) focus on the implications for the welfare gains from trade; and Asplund and Nocke (2006)
14:494:35446:20:16:71:379:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:focus on the implications for firm turnover in a dynamic setting.
14:495:35511:16:15:80:539:96:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:15See, for example, Bertoletti and Epifani (2014), Dhingra and Morrow (2014), Fabinger and Weyl (2014), Mrazova
14:496:35622:15:0:72:265:81:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:and Neary (2014), and Zhelebodko et al (2012).
15:497:35670:0:28:72:191:709:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f10:4.1  Closed Economy
15:498:35689:28:20:72:540:681:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To better highlight the role played by the properties of the demand system, we initially start with
15:499:35788:20:20:72:540:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a  closed  economy  and  analyze  the  impact  of  demand  shocks  on  product  reallocations.   We  then
15:500:35893:20:21:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:develop an open economy version of our model that meshes more closely with our empirical setup.
15:501:35988:21:20:72:540:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We show how demand shocks in an export market induce very similar product reallocations as in
15:502:36081:20:20:72:540:600:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the  closed  economy  (but  for  exporters  to  that  market).   We  develop  both  a  general  equilibrium
15:503:36188:20:21:72:540:580:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(with a single differentiated good sector for the whole economy) and a partial equilibrium version
15:504:36286:21:20:72:540:559:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:focusing on a single sector among many in the economy.  In the latter, we also introduce a short-run
15:505:36386:20:20:72:540:539:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:version where entry is restricted general equilibrium is inherently a long-run scenario).  We show
15:506:36484:20:21:72:540:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:how demand shocks induce the same skewness pattern in all of these modeling alternatives.  This
15:507:36579:21:35:72:493:498:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:highlights the critical role of the demand system in shaping the pattern of reallocations.
15:508:36669:35:28:72:342:463:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:Multi-Product Production with Additive Separable Utility
15:509:36725:28:20:72:540:435:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We  consider  a  sector  with  a  single  productive  factor,  labor.   We  will  distinguish  between  two
15:510:36832:20:20:72:540:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:scenarios.   The  first  is  the  standard  general  equilibrium  (GE)  setup  with  a  single  sector.   The
15:511:36941:20:21:72:540:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:exogenous labor endowmentLindexes both the number of workersLw(with inelastic supply) and
15:512:37030:21:20:72:540:374:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:consumersLc.   We  choose  the  endogenous  wage  as  thenumeraire.   Aggregate  expenditures  are
15:513:37128:20:20:72:540:354:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:then given by the exogenous labor endowment.  In our partial equilibrium (PE) scenario, we focus
15:514:37224:20:21:72:539:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on  the  sector  as  a  small  part  of  the  economy.   We  take  the  number  of  consumersLcas  well  as
15:515:37331:21:20:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:their  individual  expenditures  on  the  sector’s  output  as  exogenously  given.   The  supply  of  labor
15:516:37439:20:20:71:540:293:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:Lwto  the  sector  is  perfectly  elastic  at  an  exogenous  economy-wide  wage.   We  choose  units  so
15:517:37544:20:21:71:539:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that both this wage and the exogenous expenditure per-consumer is equal to 1.  This involves a
15:518:37638:21:20:71:539:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:normalization for the measure of consumersLcand the choice of labor asnumeraire:  Aggregate
15:519:37729:20:20:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:accounting then implies that this normalized number of consumersLcrepresents a fraction of the
15:520:37823:20:21:72:539:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:labor endowmentL.16In both scenarios, we model a demand shock as an increase in the number of
15:521:37916:21:20:72:539:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:consumersLc.  This increases aggregate expenditures one-for-one, given our assumptions of unitary
15:522:38013:20:16:72:540:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:consumer income.  In our GE scenario, this increase is associated with a proportional increase in
15:523:38110:16:15:80:539:155:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:16As  we  will  restrict  our  analysis  to  additively  separable  preferences  –  which  are  non-homothetic  –  changes  in
15:524:38236:15:11:72:540:140:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:consumer income will have different effects than changes in the number of consumersLc.  We focus on this functional
15:525:38351:11:11:72:540:129:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:form  for  tractability  and  do  not  wish  to  emphasize  its  properties  for  income  elasticities.   As  first  highlighted  by
15:526:38483:11:10:72:540:118:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Deaton and Muellbauer (1980), additively separable preference imply a specific relationship between price and income
15:527:38599:10:11:72:540:108:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:elasticities.   We  emphasize  the  properties  of  demand  for  those  price  elasticities.   Thus,  we  analyze  changes  in  the
15:528:38730:11:11:72:539:97:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:number of consumersLcholding their income fixed.  This is akin to indexing the preferences to a given reference
15:529:38841:11:0:72:124:86:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:income level.
16:530:38856:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:labor suppliedLw.  In our PE scenario, the labor supply response is left unrestricted, isolating the
16:531:38956:21:20:71:167:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:demand-side effects.
16:532:38976:20:20:88:539:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In both scenarios each consumer’s utility is assumed to be additively separable over a continuum
16:533:39072:20:21:71:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of imperfectly substitutable products indexed byi∈[0,M] whereMis the measure of products
16:534:39160:21:37:71:525:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:available.  The representative consumer then solves the following utility maximization problem:
16:535:39255:37:7:219:239:590:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:max
16:536:39258:7:0:221:238:583:8:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f6:qi≥0
16:537:39262:0:24:242:260:605:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f12:∫M
16:538:39264:24:0:248:252:581:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:0
16:539:39265:0:0:264:315:590:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:u(qi)dis.t.
16:540:39276:0:24:320:339:605:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f12:∫M
16:541:39278:24:0:326:330:581:8:g_d0_f6:8:g_d0_f6:0
16:542:39279:0:36:342:392:590:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:piqidi= 1,
16:543:39289:36:21:71:540:554:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:whereu(qi) is the sub-utility associated with the consumption ofqiunits of producti.  We assume
16:544:39384:21:36:71:325:533:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that this sub-utility exhibits the following properties:
16:545:39440:36:37:123:487:497:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:(A1)u(qi)≥0 with equality forqi= 0;u′(qi)>0 andu′′(qi)<0 forqi≥0.
16:546:39505:37:20:71:539:460:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The first order condition for the consumer’s problem determines theinverseresidual demand func-
16:547:39600:20:21:71:169:440:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tion (per consumer):
16:548:39620:21:0:272:305:419:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:p(qi) =
16:549:39627:0:15:309:335:427:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:u′(qi)
16:550:39633:15:0:319:325:412:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:λ
16:551:39634:0:30:336:540:419:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:,(4)
16:552:39638:30:0:72:121:389:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:whereλ=
16:553:39645:0:13:125:140:398:11:g_d0_f16:8:g_d0_f12:∫M
16:554:39647:13:0:130:149:385:8:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f11:0u
16:555:39649:0:24:149:540:393:8:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f4:′(qi)qidi >0 is the marginal utility of income.  Given our assumption of separable
16:556:39731:24:20:72:539:369:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:preferences, this marginal utility of incomeλis the unique endogenous aggregate demand shifter:
16:557:39826:20:21:72:540:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Higherλshifts all residual demand curvesinward; we refer to this as an increase in competition
16:558:39920:21:20:72:540:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for a given level of market demandLc.  Concavity ofu(qi) ensures that the chosen consumption
16:559:40012:20:20:72:540:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:level from (4) also satisfies the second order condition for the consumer’s problem.  This residual
16:560:40111:20:37:72:367:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:demand curve (4) is associated with a marginal revenue curve
16:561:40171:37:0:246:281:251:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:φ(qi) =
16:562:40178:0:15:285:360:258:11:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f12:u′(qi) +u′′(qi)qi
16:563:40195:15:0:320:326:243:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f11:λ
16:564:40196:0:37:362:540:251:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:.(5)
16:565:40200:37:20:72:539:214:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Letεp(qi)≡ −p′(qi)qi/p(qi) andεφ(qi)≡ −φ′(qi)qi/φ(qi) denote the elasticities of inverse demand
16:566:40295:20:21:72:540:194:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and marginal revenue (expressed in absolute values).  Thusεp(qi)≥0 is the inverse price elasticity
16:567:40393:21:20:72:540:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of demand (less than 1 for elastic demand).  Although the demand and marginal revenue curves are
16:568:40489:20:20:72:539:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:residual (they depend onλ), their elasticities are nonetheless independent ofλ.  These preferences
16:569:40587:20:21:72:539:133:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:nest  the  C.E.S.  case  where  the  elasticitiesεp(qi)  andεφ(qi)  are  constant;  using  the  additively
16:570:40693:21:20:72:540:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:separable functional form for C.E.S., the marginal utility of incomeλis then an inverse monotone
16:571:40789:20:20:72:236:92:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:function of the C.E.S. price index.
16:572:40824:20:0:88:539:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Products  are  supplied  by  firms  that  may  be  single-  or  multi-product.   Market  structure  is
17:573:40928:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:monopolistically competitive as in Mayer, Melitz and Ottaviano (2014):  each product is supplied
17:574:41024:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by  a  single  firm  and  each  firm  supplies  a  countable  number  of  products  (among  the  continuum
17:575:41130:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  consumed  products).   Technology  exhibits  increasing  returns  to  scale  associated  with  a  fixed
17:576:41237:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:overhead cost, along with a constant marginal cost of production.  We assume that the fixed cost
17:577:41333:21:20:72:540:627:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:fis common for all products while the marginal costv(variety level cost) is heterogeneous.  For
17:578:41428:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a given firm,  products are indexed in increasing ordermof marginal cost from a ‘core product’
17:579:41522:20:21:72:539:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:indexed bym= 0.  Firm entry incurs a sunk costfe.  After this cost is incurred, entrants randomly
17:580:41619:21:20:72:540:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:draw the marginal cost for their core product from a common continuous differentiable distribution
17:581:41717:20:20:72:539:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Γ(c) with support over [0,∞);  we refer to this cost draw as the firm’s core competency.17This
17:582:41811:20:21:72:540:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:gives an entrant the exclusive blueprint used to produce a countable range of additional products
17:583:41908:21:20:72:540:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:indexed by the integerm(potentially zero) at marginal costv(m,c)≡cz(m) withz(0) = 1 and
17:584:41995:20:36:72:129:485:11:g_d0_f11:8:g_d0_f6:z′(m)>0.18

17:597:42905:15:11:72:540:142:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:without any firm selection.  We could also introduce an upper-bound cost draw so long as this upper-bound is high
17:598:43018:11:7:72:378:131:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:enough that the equilibrium features selection (some firms do not produce).

20:720:48580:20:16:71:202:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the varieties they produce).
20:721:48608:16:15:80:539:284:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:20This sector-level adjustment for labor supply is very similar to the case of C.E.S. product differentiation within
20:722:48724:15:11:72:540:269:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:sectors and Cobb-Douglas preferences across sectors.  In the latter case, the sector’s labor supply adjusts so that it

20:724:48955:11:7:72:464:247:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:sector.  See Melitz & Redding (2014) for an example of those preferences with firm heterogeneity.
20:725:49052:7:15:80:539:240:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:21Competitionλmust strictly increase for the free entry condition to hold.  Ifλdecreased (even weakly), then net

20:727:49272:11:11:72:540:214:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:then strictly increase (given 11);  along with the average firm profit (the left-hand-side) in the free-entry condition
20:728:49391:11:7:72:329:203:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:(12).  Thus, this condition could not hold ifλweakly decreased.
20:729:49454:7:15:80:540:196:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:22Competitionλmust  strictly  increase  in  order  to  satisfy  the  budget  constraint  (13)  with  a  fixed  number  of
20:730:49575:15:11:72:539:181:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:incumbents.   As  we  argued  in  a  previous  footnote  (21),λweakly  decreasing  would  imply  a  strict  increase  in  the
20:731:49700:11:11:72:540:170:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:cutoffs ˆv= ˆc.  This would entail both a strict increase in the number of products consumed as well as a weak increase
20:732:49819:11:11:72:540:159:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:in  expenditures  per-productr(v,λ)  for  each  consumer  (recall  thatεr,λ<0).   This  would  necessarily  violate  the
20:733:49939:11:7:72:193:148:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:consumer’s budget constraint.
20:734:49968:7:15:80:539:141:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:23Note  that  with  a  fixed  number  of  incumbents,  the  budget  constraint  (13)  implies  an  increasing  relationship
20:735:50091:15:0:72:533:126:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:between the cutoff ˆcand the level of competitionλ(which reduces product-level revenuesr(v,λ) for all products).
21:736:50205:0:28:72:176:709:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:Curvature of Demand
21:737:50224:28:20:72:540:681:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Up to now, we have placed very few restrictions on the shape of the residual demand curves that the
21:738:50323:20:20:72:540:661:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:firms face, other than the conditions (A1)-(A3) needed to ensure a unique monopolistic competition
21:739:50421:20:21:72:540:641:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equilibrium.  In particular, the rates of change of the elasticities of residual demand and marginal
21:740:50521:21:20:72:539:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:revenue (the signs ofε′p(qi) andε′φ(qi)) were left unrestricted.  We now show how further restrictions
21:741:50623:20:20:71:539:600:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on  those  rates  of  change  (or  alternatively  the  curvature  of  demand  and  marginal  revenue)  are
21:742:50729:20:21:71:539:580:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:intrinsically tied to product-level reallocations – in addition to their better known consequences
21:743:50827:21:20:71:539:559:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for prices, markups and pass-through.  After we develop the open economy version of our model in
21:744:50923:20:20:71:539:539:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the next section, we highlight the reverse connection from the pattern of product reallocations we
21:745:51021:20:21:71:539:519:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:documented in Section 3 back to their necessary conditions for demand.  Throughout, we assume
21:746:51114:21:20:71:539:498:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f9:that  conditions  (A1)-(A3)  hold  in  our  monopolistic  competition  equilibrium.   Thus,  anecessary
21:747:51217:20:20:72:540:478:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:condition  for  an  empirical  pattern  is  anadditionalcondition  that  must  hold  (to  generate  that
21:748:51321:20:21:72:368:458:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:empirical prediction)conditionalon those initial assumptions.
21:749:51382:21:36:88:450:437:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The further restrictions on the shapes of demand and marginal revenue are:
21:750:51456:36:37:242:369:401:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f11:(B1)ε′p(qi)>0 forqi≥0,
21:751:51478:37:21:72:90:364:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and
21:752:51481:21:30:240:371:343:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f11:(B1’)ε′φ(qi)>0 forqi≥0.
21:753:51504:30:20:71:539:313:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure  1  depicts  a  log-log  graph  of  the  inverse  demand  and  marginal  revenue  curves  satisfying
21:754:51611:20:20:71:539:293:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:those  restrictions.   Under  (B1)  demand  becomes  more  inelastic  with  consumption.   This  is  also
21:755:51716:20:21:71:539:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:known as Marshall’s Second Law of Demand.24It is a necessary and sufficient condition for better
21:756:51812:21:20:71:540:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:performing products (lowerv) to have higher markups and for tougher competition (higherλ) to
21:757:51904:20:16:72:540:232:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lower markups for any given product (given a costv).25Thus, the evidence discussed in Section
21:758:51997:16:15:80:539:216:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:24We  thank  Peter  Neary  for  bringing  this  reference  to  our  attention.   (B1)  is  equivalent  to  the  assumption  by
21:759:52123:15:11:72:540:201:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Arkolakis et al (2015) that the demand function of any product is log-concave in log-prices.  In the terminology of
21:760:52238:11:11:72:540:190:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Neary and Mrazova (2014) it defines the “sub-convex” case, with “sub-convexity” of an inverse demand function at
21:761:52350:11:11:72:540:179:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:an  arbitrary  point  being  equivalent  to  the  function  being  less  convex  at  that  point  than  a  CES  demand  function
21:762:52478:11:11:72:540:168:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:with the same elasticity.  In the terminology of Zhelobodko et al (2012), this class of preferences exhibits increasing
21:763:52597:11:11:72:540:157:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:“relative love of variety” (RLV) as consumers care more about variety when their consumption level is higher.  In the
21:764:52714:11:11:72:540:146:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:terminology of Kimball (1995), this class of preferences exhibits a positive superelasticity of demand.  Bertoletti and
21:765:52833:11:11:72:540:135:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:Epifani (2014) refer to this case as “decreasing elasticity of substitution”.  The “Adjustable pass-through” (APT) class
21:766:52953:11:11:72:540:124:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:of demand functions proposed by Fabinger and Weyl (2012) also satisfies (B1).  Lastly, condition (B1) is sufficient
21:767:53068:11:11:72:540:113:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:for the induced maximized profit function to exhibit all the properties postulated by Asplund and Nocke (2006) in
21:768:53181:11:11:72:540:102:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:order to explain the empirical relationship between market size and firm turnover that they document (in a dynamic
21:769:53295:11:7:72:105:91:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:setting).
21:770:53304:7:0:80:434:84:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:25Since both higher costvand higherλis associated with lower outputq(v,λ); See (8).
22:771:53389:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:2, linking better product and firm performance to higher markups implies that (B1) must hold.  It
22:772:53486:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is also consistent with the estimates of Arkolakis et al (2015) for bilateral trade demand.  In our
22:773:53585:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model with monopolistic competition, (B1) is also equivalent to an alternate condition that the pass-
22:774:53686:20:21:72:540:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:through elasticity from marginal cost to priceθ≡∂lnp(q(v,λ))/∂lnv=εp/εφis less than 1 (see
22:775:53776:21:20:71:539:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:appendix for proof).  Thus, the vast empirical evidence on incomplete pass-through (see the survey
22:776:53874:20:20:71:539:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by Burstein and Gopinath, 2014) also requires demand condition (B1).  Most importantly, we will
22:777:53969:20:21:71:539:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:show that (B1) is a necessary condition for the evidence we documented on product reallocations
22:778:54064:21:20:71:539:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for French exporters.  This provides an independent confirmation for this demand condition that
22:779:54159:20:20:71:539:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:does not rely on the (very noisy) measurement of product prices and the estimation of markups
22:780:54252:20:31:71:228:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(or alternatively marginal costs).

23:795:55345:0:21:72:540:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the evidence on such pass-through differences that we previously discussed (for French,  Belgian,
23:796:55442:21:20:72:540:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Brazilian, and Chinese firms/products).  In the following section, we show that (B1’) is a sufficient
23:797:55543:20:20:72:540:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:condition for the product reallocations we previously described for French exporters, in addition to
23:798:55643:20:21:72:473:648:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:all the evidence from the existing literature on prices, markups, and pass-through.26
23:799:55728:21:20:88:539:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Lastly we note that conditions (B1) and (B1’) exclude the C.E.S. case, where the derivative of
23:800:55822:20:20:72:540:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the elasticitiesε′p(qi) andε′p(qi) are zero.  In this limiting case, the inverse demand and marginal

23:804:56147:35:28:72:274:511:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:Demand Shocks and Product Reallocations
23:805:56186:28:20:72:539:483:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We have already described how an increase in demandLcinduces an increase in the toughness of
23:806:56278:20:20:71:539:463:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:competitionλin both the long-run (GE and PE) and the short-run.  We now highlight how the
23:807:56367:20:21:71:539:443:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:demand conditions (B1) and (B1’) generate a link between increases in the toughness of competition
23:808:56465:21:20:71:370:422:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and product reallocations towards better performing products.
23:809:56526:20:20:88:540:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:First,  we  note  that  the  increase  in  competitionλinduces  a  downward  shift  in  output  sales
23:810:56627:20:21:71:540:382:11:g_d0_f11:11:g_d0_f4:q(v,λ)  per-consumer  (though  not  necessarily  overall  as  the  number  of  consumers  is  increasing).
23:811:56733:21:20:71:540:361:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This decrease in output salesq(v,λ) in turn generates changes in the price and marginal revenue
23:812:56828:20:20:71:539:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:elasticitiesεpandεφ, which depend on conditions (B1) and (B1’).  Changes in those two elasticities
23:813:56926:20:21:71:539:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:then determine the changes in the elasticities of output, sales, and profit with respect to marginal
23:814:57026:21:20:71:539:300:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:costv(see 8-10), which govern the reallocation of output, sales, and profit across firms with different
23:815:57129:20:27:71:532:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:costsv.  We can now determine exactly how conditions (B1) and (B1’) affect these reallocations:
23:816:57224:27:20:71:539:253:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f9:Proposition 1(B1) is a necessary and sufficient condition for a positive demand shock to reallo-
23:817:57320:20:28:71:535:233:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:cate operating profits to better performing products:π(v1,λ)/π(v2,λ)increases wheneverv1< v2.
23:818:57413:28:20:88:540:205:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f4:Proof.|επ,v|increases for all productsvwheneverλincreases if and only ifεp(qi) is increasing
23:819:57505:20:30:71:108:185:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(see 10)
23:820:57513:30:20:72:539:155:11:g_d0_f10:11:g_d0_f9:Proposition 2(B1’)  is  a  necessary  and  sufficient  condition  for  a  positive  demand  shock  to  real-
23:821:57621:20:16:72:493:135:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f9:locate output to better performing products:q(v1,λ)/q(v2,λ)increases wheneverv1< v2.
23:822:57705:16:15:80:539:119:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:26We  will  also  show  how  the  necessary  condition  for  the  French  exporters  evidence  on  product  reallocations  is
23:823:57830:15:7:72:209:104:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:slightly less restrictive than (B1’).
23:824:57867:7:15:80:539:97:6:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f8:27Those functional forms include quadratic (linear demand),  Bulow-Pfleiderer,  CARA, and bipower preferences.
23:825:57977:15:11:72:540:82:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:In a separate Appendix, we review those functional forms and describe the parameter restrictions associated with
23:826:58089:11:0:72:179:71:9:g_d0_f8:9:g_d0_f8:conditions (B1) and (B1’).

24:833:58533:20:21:72:430:563:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f6:is decreasing (see 10).  (B1’) implies that [1−εp(qi)]/εφ(qi) is decreasing.28
24:834:58611:21:20:88:539:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We have derived these reallocations using the per-consumer measures of performance, but since
24:835:58704:20:20:72:540:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:they are all evaluated as ratios, multiplying those by the number of consumersLcwould lead to
24:836:58797:20:21:72:540:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identical outcomes (even thoughLcis changing).  Thus, we see that (B1’) is a sufficient condition
24:837:58894:21:20:72:540:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for all performance measures (profit, output, revenue) to be reallocated toward better performing
24:838:58991:20:20:72:539:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:products.  In this case, an increase in competition (higherλ) induces a steeper relationship between
24:839:59091:20:21:72:539:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a product’s costvand its profit, output, and revenue outcome (higher elasticities|επ,v|,|εq,v|,|εr,v|).
24:840:59194:21:20:72:540:420:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A given percentage reduction in costvthen translates into a higher percentage increase in those
24:841:59289:20:20:72:540:400:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:performance outcomes.  In the case of C.E.S. preferences, all those performance elasticities would
24:842:59387:20:21:72:540:380:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be constant, and hence changes in demand (and corresponding changes in competitionλ) would
24:843:59477:21:20:72:535:359:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:have no effect on the relative performance of products (conditional on selection into production).
24:844:59575:20:20:88:539:339:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The reallocation of output towards better performing products has a direct consequence for firm
24:845:59670:20:21:72:540:319:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:productivity:  the allocation of firm employment to products must respond proportionately to the
24:846:59766:21:20:72:540:298:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:product-level output changes.  Thus, for a given set of products, average productivity (an employ-
24:847:59864:20:20:72:539:278:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ment weighted average of product productivity 1/v) must increase whenever output is reallocated
24:848:59959:20:36:72:246:258:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:towards better performing products.
